<p><b>Sadio Mané</b> (born 10 April 1992) is a Senegalese professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegal national team</a>. Regarded as one of the best players in the world, Mané finished fourth for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Ballon_d%27Or" title="2019 Ballon d&#39;Or">2019 Ballon d'Or</a>, and in the award for the <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Men%27s_Player" title="The Best FIFA Men&#39;s Player">Best FIFA Men's Player</a> he ranked fifth in <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2019#The_Best_FIFA_Men&#39;s_Player" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2019">2019</a> and fourth in <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2020#The_Best_FIFA_Men&#39;s_Player" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2020">2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballon_dor_2019-12-02_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballon_dor_2019-12-02-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mané began his professional career with <a href="/wiki/Ligue_2" title="Ligue 2">Ligue 2</a> club <a href="/wiki/FC_Metz" title="FC Metz">Metz</a> at age 19, but he departed after a solitary season to join Austrian club <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</a> in 2012 for a fee of 4&#160;million, winning a <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Football_Bundesliga" title="Austrian Football Bundesliga">league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Cup" title="Austrian Cup">cup</a> domestic double in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg_season" title="201314 FC Red Bull Salzburg season">201314 season</a>. Later that summer, Mané transferred to English club <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> for a club record fee of £11.8&#160;million. There, he set a new <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_records_and_statistics" title="Premier League records and statistics">record</a> for the fastest <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a>, scored in 176 seconds in a 61 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-trick_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trick-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>He signed for fellow Premier League side Liverpool in 2016, for a reported fee of £34&#160;million. With Liverpool, Mané helped them reach back-to-back <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Champions League Final">UEFA Champions League Finals</a> in <a href="/wiki/2018_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2018 UEFA Champions League Final">2018</a> and <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019</a>, winning the latter. He also finished as the league's joint-top goalscorer in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Premier_League" title="201819 Premier League">201819 season</a>, winning the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a>. Mané then helped end Liverpool's <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Liverpool_F.C._season" title="201920 Liverpool F.C. season">30 year league title drought</a> by winning the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Premier_League" title="201920 Premier League">201920 Premier League</a>.
</p><p>At international level, Mané has registered 21 goals in 71 <a href="/wiki/Cap_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cap (association football)">appearances</a> for Senegal since his debut in 2012, and currently ranks as his nation's <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team#Player_records" title="Senegal national football team">third all-time top goalscorer, and joint sixth all-time for appearances</a>. He represented Senegal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics  Men&#39;s tournament">2012 Olympics</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2017 Africa Cup of Nations">2017</a> editions of the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">Africa Cup of Nations</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations">2019</a> iteration, Mané helped Senegal to a runners-up finish, and a year later, was named <a href="/wiki/African_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="African Footballer of the Year">African Footballer of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian070120_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian070120-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Mané also represented his nation at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>, in their second ever appearance in the competition.
</p><p>Mané was cited as one of the Top 100 most influential Africans by <a href="/wiki/New_African" title="New African">New African</a> magazine in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9dhiou" title="Sédhiou">Sédhiou</a>, Sénégal, Mané started his career at the Académie Génération Foot, Senegalese football academy.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mané made his professional debut for <a href="/wiki/FC_Metz" title="FC Metz">Metz</a> on 14 January 2012, coming on as a <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9vin_Diaz_(footballer_born_1988)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kévin Diaz (footballer born 1988)">Kévin Diaz</a> in the 75th minute of a 01 home defeat against <a href="/wiki/SC_Bastia" title="SC Bastia">Bastia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ligue_2" title="Ligue 2">Ligue 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He made 19 appearances in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Ligue_2" title="201112 Ligue 2">his first league season</a>, 12 as a starter, and scored a solitary goal in a 25 loss to <a href="/wiki/EA_Guingamp" class="mw-redirect" title="EA Guingamp">Guingamp</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Saint-Symphorien" title="Stade Saint-Symphorien">Stade Saint-Symphorien</a> on 4 May.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Metz were <a href="/wiki/Relegation" class="mw-redirect" title="Relegation">relegated</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Championnat_National" title="Championnat National">Championnat National</a> at the end of the season.
</p><p>During his time with Metz, he was teammates with <a href="/wiki/Kalidou_Koulibaly" title="Kalidou Koulibaly">Kalidou Koulibaly</a>, who at the time did not have a Senegalese passport and was playing international football for the French <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-20_football_team" title="France national under-20 football team">U-20</a> team.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Bull_Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG/220px-RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG/330px-RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG/440px-RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2376" data-file-height="1735" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RBS_gegen_Metz59.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mané (right) playing for <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</a> in 2013</div></div></div>
<p>On 31 August 2012, Mané moved to <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Football_Bundesliga" title="Austrian Football Bundesliga">Austrian Bundesliga</a> side <a href="/wiki/FC_Red_Bull_Salzburg" title="FC Red Bull Salzburg">Red Bull Salzburg</a> for the third biggest transfer fee that <a href="/wiki/FC_Metz" title="FC Metz">FC Metz</a> had ever received.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The fee was believed to be 4&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He scored his first <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> for the club on 31 October, in a 31 away win at <a href="/w/index.php?title=SC_Kalsdorf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SC Kalsdorf (page does not exist)">Kalsdorf</a> in the third round of the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Cup" title="Austrian Cup">Austrian Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 October 2013, he netted his first hat-trick in the Austrian Bundesliga, during a 30 win away to <a href="/wiki/SV_Gr%C3%B6dig" title="SV Grödig">Grödig</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He scored another treble on 7 May 2014 as Salzburg won 70 at <a href="/wiki/SV_Horn" title="SV Horn">Horn</a> in the cup semi-finals;<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> the season ended with the team winning a domestic <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">double</a>. At the end of August 2014 Mané forced a transfer out of the club, by not coming to the training and to the most important game for Salzburg at that time to qualify for the Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southampton">Southampton</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201415_season">201415 season</span></h4>
<p>On 1 September 2014, Mané transferred to <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> side <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> for £11.8&#160;million, signing a four-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut 22 days later in a 21 <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>, winning the penalty for Southampton's first goal.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He made his first league appearance for the club in another 21 victory over <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> on 27 September, starting and assisting <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Bertrand" title="Ryan Bertrand">Ryan Bertrand</a> for the first goal of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for the club in an 80 victory over <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> on 18 October,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> although this was subsequently credited as an own goal by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_van_Aanholt" title="Patrick van Aanholt">Patrick van Aanholt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> He did, however, score his first goal in his next game, a 10 win over <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> a week later.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December and January he scored in three successive matches, against <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Mané scored two late winning goals in 10 league victories at <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> on 7 February 2015 and at home to <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> on 3 March respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> However, Mané had been dropped from Southampton's starting line-up for their 02 home defeat to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> on 22 February as a punishment for being late to the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 May, during Southampton's final home match of the season, Mané scored three times in 2 minutes 56 seconds in a 61 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> to set a new <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_records_and_statistics" title="Premier League records and statistics">Premier League record</a> for the fastest <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a>. The record had been held since 1994 by <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>, who scored three against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in 4 minutes and 33 seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-trick_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trick-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Mané finished the season with 10 goals from 32 appearances in all competitions.
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201516_season">201516 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG/220px-Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG/330px-Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG/440px-Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2679" data-file-height="1431" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Audi-_quattro-Cup_23.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mané (right) playing for <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> in 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Mané began the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Southampton_F.C._season" title="201516 Southampton F.C. season">201516 season</a> by registering two assists in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League" title="201516 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> third qualifying round first leg match with <a href="/wiki/Vitesse_Arnhem" class="mw-redirect" title="Vitesse Arnhem">Vitesse Arnhem</a> at home and scoring in the return leg, as Southampton eased through to the next round 50 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 2 December, he took 39 seconds to open the scoring against Liverpool in the quarter-finals of the League Cup, but the Saints eventually lost 61 at home.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 January 2016, he was again dropped from the starting line-up by manager <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a> for a match at <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> when he turned up late for a pre-match meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He received a straight red card on 12 March at the end of a 21 win at <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoke City">Stoke City</a> for a collision into <a href="/wiki/Erik_Pieters" title="Erik Pieters">Erik Pieters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> although this was quickly overturned on appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having failed to score in the league for over four months, Mané scored twice in a 32 victory over <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> on 20 March 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> followed by five goals in the next five matches, including a hat-trick in a 42 victory against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on 1 May.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He finished the season as Southampton's top scorer, with 15 goals in all competitions.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liverpool">Liverpool</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201617_season">201617 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liver-SM_2017_(11_cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg/170px-Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg/255px-Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg/340px-Liver-SM_2017_%2811_cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="842" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liver-SM_2017_(11_cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mané playing for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>On 28 June 2016, Mané joined <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> for a transfer fee of £34&#160;million on a five-year contract. The transfer fee made him the most expensive African player in history at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC36642523_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC36642523-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August, he made his <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> debut for the Reds, scoring the fourth goal in a 43 away win against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Having missed Liverpool's defeat at <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> through a slight shoulder injury, Mané returned to the starting line-up against <a href="/wiki/Burton_Albion_F.C." title="Burton Albion F.C.">Burton Albion</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_EFL_Cup" title="201617 EFL Cup">League Cup</a> where he had two assists in a 50 win.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 December, Mané scored the only goal of the 227th <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_derby" title="Merseyside derby">Merseyside derby</a> in added time against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> at <a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">Goodison Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
On 11 February 2017, Mané scored two goals within two minutes against <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur" class="mw-redirect" title="Tottenham Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</a> at Anfield, for Liverpool's first league win in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April 2017, Mané was named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> after scoring 13 league goals in his first season with Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1617_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1617-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Despite missing the latter part of the campaign through injury, Mané was awarded the Liverpool <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C.#Player_of_the_Season" title="Liverpool F.C.">Player of the Season</a> award on 9 May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201718_season">201718 season</span></h4>
<p>In the first match of the new season, on 12 August 2017, away to <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, Mané scored Liverpool's first goal of the season in a 33 draw. He was named <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> after scoring a goal in each of the Reds' three matches in August.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 9 September 2017, he was given a straight red card in the first half of a 50 loss to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> for a high boot against goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Ederson_Moraes" class="mw-redirect" title="Ederson Moraes">Ederson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a three-match ban.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Mané, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Salah" title="Mohamed Salah">Mohamed Salah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Firmino" title="Roberto Firmino">Roberto Firmino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Coutinho" title="Philippe Coutinho">Philippe Coutinho</a> made up a prolific attacking quartet dubbed the "Fab Four" and "Fab Three" after the mid-season exit of the latter.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 February 2018, Mané scored his first <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_hat-tricks" title="List of UEFA Champions League hat-tricks">hat-trick</a> for Liverpool in a 50 away win against <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League_knockout_phase" title="201718 UEFA Champions League knockout phase">round of 16</a> first leg of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League" title="201718 UEFA Champions League">201718 UEFA Champions League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, he became only the second player to score an away hat-trick for the club in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Later, with a goal in the 30 win over <a href="/wiki/AFC_Bournemouth" title="AFC Bournemouth">AFC Bournemouth</a> on 14 April, he overtook <a href="/wiki/Demba_Ba" title="Demba Ba">Demba Ba</a>'s record of 43 to become the highest scoring Senegalese in Premier League history.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 May, during the <a href="/wiki/2018_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2018 UEFA Champions League Final">2018 UEFA Champions League Final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a>, Mané scored Liverpool's equalising goal in a 31 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In doing so, he became the first Senegalese player to score in the final of the competition. His goal was also his 10th for the campaign which saw Liverpool become the first team in history to have three players score 10+ goals in a single Champions League season, with Mané achieving the milestone alongside fellow <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forwards</a> Salah and Firmino.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.9319_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201819_season">201819 season</span></h4>
<p>On 22 November 2018, Mané signed new long-term deal with the Reds.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On 10 March 2019, Mané scored twice in a 42 win over Burnley, the second of which was his 50th competitive goal for Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> His goals also saw him become only the fifth Liverpool player to score in six consecutive home Premier League appearances after <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Luis Suárez">Luis Suárez</a> and Salah.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, he scored twice more in a 31 win over <a href="/wiki/Bayern_Munich" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> to help Liverpool progress to the quarter-finals of the Champions League. In doing so, he became the club's record goalscorer away from home in the competition with seven goals to his name.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> During Liverpool's next match, he broke another of Ba's records to become the Senegalese player with the most goals scored in a single Premier League season, after scoring his 17th goal for the campaign in a 21 win over <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> On 20 April, he was one of six players nominated for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Players%27_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Players&#39; Player of the Year">PFA Players' Player of the Year</a> award alongside teammate <a href="/wiki/Virgil_van_Dijk" title="Virgil van Dijk">Virgil van Dijk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He was also named in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a> alongside Liverpool teammates, <a href="/wiki/Trent_Alexander-Arnold" title="Trent Alexander-Arnold">Trent Alexander-Arnold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Robertson" title="Andrew Robertson">Andrew Robertson</a> and Van Dijk.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the final day of the domestic campaign, Mané scored twice in a 20 win over <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a>. His brace took him to 22 goals for the campaign which saw him share the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a> award with Salah and Arsenal's <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Emerick_Aubameyang" title="Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang">Pierre-Emerick Aubameyang</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On 1 June, Mané helped win an early penalty for Liverpool in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">2019 UEFA Champions League Final</a> against Tottenham, only 24 seconds after the kick-off, after his cross was judged to have hit <a href="/wiki/Moussa_Sissoko" title="Moussa Sissoko">Moussa Sissoko</a>'s arm inside the penalty area; Salah subsequently converted from the spot to open the scoring, and Liverpool ultimately won the match 20 to claim the title.<sup id="cite_ref-201819UCL_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201819UCL-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2019.E2.80.9320_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="201920_season">201920 season</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_(UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019)_52.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg/180px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg/270px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg/360px-FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_%28UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019%29_52.jpg 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="1099" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FC_Salzburg_gegen_Liverpool_FC_(UEFA_Champions_League_10.Dezember_2019)_52.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mané playing for Liverpool in the UEFA Champions League, December 2019</div></div></div>
<p>On 14 August 2019, Mané scored twice in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2019 UEFA Super Cup">2019 UEFA Super Cup</a> final against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in a match that Liverpool won 54 on penalties after the game had finished 22 after 120 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Mané was named man of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Exactly one month later, he scored twice in a 31 win over <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> and extended his record run of matches without defeat for Liverpool at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> to 50 matches, a league record by any player at a particular stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On his 100th Premier League appearance for Liverpool on 5 October, Mané scored his 50th league goal for the club in a 21 win over <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 October, Mané was named in the 30-man shortlist for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Ballon_d%27Or" title="2019 Ballon d&#39;Or">2019 Ballon d'Or</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On 2 December he finished in fourth place for the award, behind <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a>, Liverpool teammate <a href="/wiki/Virgil_van_Dijk" title="Virgil van Dijk">Virgil van Dijk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballon_dor_2019-12-02_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballon_dor_2019-12-02-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, he scored once and assisted two more goals as Liverpool beat Everton 52 in the Merseyside derby to extend their unbeaten run in league football to 32 matches, which was a new club record.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, Liverpool won the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2019 FIFA Club World Cup">2019 FIFA Club World Cup</a>, with Mané setting up the winning goal scored by Firmino in the <a href="/wiki/2019_FIFA_Club_World_Cup_Final" title="2019 FIFA Club World Cup Final">final</a> against <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 January 2020, Mané was named the CAF <a href="/wiki/African_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="African Footballer of the Year">African Footballer of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian070120_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian070120-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> He is only the second Senegalese after <a href="/wiki/El_Hadji_Diouf" title="El Hadji Diouf">El Hadji Diouf</a> to have won this award.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 February, Mané scored the winner in a 32 home win against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> in the Premier League as Liverpool made it 21 consecutive home wins, a league record shared with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Shankly" title="Bill Shankly">Bill Shankly</a>'s Liverpool team from 1972, and also made it a joint Premier League record 18 wins in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On 7 March, Mané scored the winning goal in a 21 win against Bournemouth at Anfield as Liverpool set a new <a href="/wiki/Football_records_and_statistics_in_England#Wins" title="Football records and statistics in England">English top-flight record</a> of 22 consecutive home wins.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Liverpool went on to win the Premier League title at the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="202021_season">202021 season</span></h4>
<p>On 20 September 2020, Mané opened his scoring account in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Premier_League" title="202021 Premier League">202021 Premier League</a> with both Liverpool goals in a 20 win away to Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> On 2 October 2020, Mané tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<p>Mané was part of the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_under-23_football_team" title="Senegal national under-23 football team">Senegal team</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics  Men&#39;s tournament">2012 Olympic tournament</a>, and started every match as they advanced through <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament_%E2%80%93_Group_A" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics  Men&#39;s tournament  Group A">Group A</a> as runners-up to <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Britain national football team">Great Britain</a> before losing 42 after extra time in the quarter-finals to eventual champions <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_under-23_football_team" title="Mexico national under-23 football team">Mexico</a>.
</p><p>Mané was ruled out of the <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">Senegalese squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">2015 Africa Cup of Nations</a> after suffering a calf injury in Southampton's 20 win against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> on 1 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He later returned to the squad, and started in their final two group matches against <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_football_team" title="South Africa national football team">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_Group_C" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations Group C">group stage exit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mané represented Senegal at the <a href="/wiki/2017_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2017 Africa Cup of Nations">2017 Africa Cup of Nations</a> in Gabon and scored a goal in each of the nation's opening two games, 20 wins against <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_national_football_team" title="Zimbabwe national football team">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> After a goalless draw in the quarter-final clash against <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a>, he missed the penalty in the shoot-out that saw Senegal eliminated from the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2018, Mané was named in Senegal's 23-man squad for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> He scored the opening goal in a 22 draw against <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_Group_H" title="2018 FIFA World Cup Group H">group stage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Mané started all three of Senegal's group matches as they were eliminated after the first stage, finishing below Japan on fair play points.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mané was once again called up to Senegal's final squad for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations">2019 Africa Cup of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> He scored two goals and missed a penalty in a 30 win against <a href="/wiki/Kenya_national_football_team" title="Kenya national football team">Kenya</a>, as Senegal finished second in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_Group_C" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations Group C">group stage</a> and qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_knockout_stage" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations knockout stage">knockout stage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Mané scored the only goal of the match and missed another penalty in Senegal's 10 win over <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_football_team" title="Uganda national football team">Uganda</a> in the round of 16.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> He played in Senegal's next three matches as they advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations_Final" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations Final">final</a>, losing 10 to Algeria in a rematch of Senegal's opening game of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Despite finishing the competition as runner-up, Mané was named to the <a href="/wiki/2019_Africa_Cup_of_Nations#CAF_AFCON_Team_of_the_Tournament" title="2019 Africa Cup of Nations">Team of the Tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFCON_TOTY_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFCON_TOTY-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_(9).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg/220px-Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg/330px-Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg/440px-Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_%289%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="829" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spartak_Moscow_VS._Liverpool_(9).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mané with Liverpool in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Mané was described as a complete player who plays with 'high levels of intensity and concentration' by Liverpool teammate <a href="/wiki/Fabinho_(footballer,_born_1993)" title="Fabinho (footballer, born 1993)">Fabinho</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Former Liverpool defender <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Carragher" title="Jamie Carragher">Jamie Carragher</a> called Mané a "world-class winger", comparing him to the likes of former Liverpool player <a href="/wiki/John_Barnes_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Barnes (footballer)">John Barnes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He was compared to <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> by former Ajax defender <a href="/wiki/Danny_Blind" title="Danny Blind">Danny Blind</a>, who praised him for his ability to score with either foot and headers, along with making "astonishing" sprints.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> A versatile forward, Mané is a prolific goalscorer, whose main traits are his finishing, speed, technique, and trickery in possession, as well as his decision-making, tactical awareness, creativity, agility, balance, control, touch on the ball, and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> skills.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rumours_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rumours-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-quiet_kid_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quiet_kid-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-terrifying_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terrifying-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>&lt;<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He has drawn praise in the media for his intelligent play, passing, and his ability to get into good positions, from which he can score goals or create chances for teammates.<sup id="cite_ref-rumours_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rumours-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-quiet_kid_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quiet_kid-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Known for his quiet and timid personality, his ability to cope with pressure has also been highlighted as one of his main strengths.<sup id="cite_ref-quiet_kid_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quiet_kid-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Beyond his offensive, technical, and creative qualities, his high defensive work-rate has also been noted by pundits, as well as his ability in the air, despite his modest stature of 1.75m (5' 9").<sup id="cite_ref-terrifying_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terrifying-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Mané usually plays as a winger on the left flank, a position which allows him to cut into the centre and shoot on goal with his stronger, right foot.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Mané pursued a career in football despite his father forbidding him from playing the sport as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> He currently resides in <a href="/wiki/Allerton,_Liverpool" title="Allerton, Liverpool">Allerton</a> and has been burgled twice, once in November 2017 and again in February 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> He is a practising <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> and occasionally is seen making <a href="/wiki/Dua" title="Dua">du'a</a> before the start of each match.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
